2:25:1478:0:14:72:537:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:F:Sorting or Steering: Experimental Evidence on the Economic Effects of Housing Discrimination 
2:26:1570:14:14:72:283:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:Peter Christensen and Christopher Timmins
2:27:1611:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 24826
2:28:1639:14:14:72:119:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:July 2018
2:29:1648:14:28:72:182:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:JEL No. Q51,Q53,R31
2:30:1667:28:28:274:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:F:ABSTRACT
2:31:1675:28:14:71:545:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:Housing  discrimination  is  illegal.  However,  paired-tester  audit  experiments  have  revealed 
2:32:1774:14:14:71:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:evidence of  discrimination  in  the  interactions  between  potential  buyers  and  real  estate  agents, 
2:33:1880:14:14:71:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:raising  concern about  whether  certain  groups  are  systematically  excluded  from  the  beneficial 
2:34:1982:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:effects  of  healthy  neighborhoods. Using  data  from  HUD’s  most  recent  Housing  Discrimination 
2:35:2082:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:Study  and  micro-level  data  on  key  attributes of  neighborhoods  in  28  US  cities,  we  find  strong 
2:36:2189:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:evidence of discrimination in the characteristics of neighborhoods towards which individuals are 
2:37:2285:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:steered. Conditional upon the characteristics of the house suggested by the audit tester, minorities 
2:38:2385:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:are significantly more likely to be steered towards neighborhoods with less economic opportunity 
2:39:2481:14:14:72:546:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:and  greater  exposures  to  crime  and  local  pollutants.  We  find  that  holding locational  preferences 
2:40:2589:14:14:72:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:or   income   constant,   discriminatory   steering   alone   can   contribute   substantially to   the 
2:41:2692:14:14:72:545:448:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:F:disproportionate  number  of  minority  households  found  in  high  poverty  neighborhoods  in  the 
2:42:2792:14:14:72:546:434:12:Times:12:Times:F:United  States.  The  steering  effect  is  also  large  enough  to  fully  explain  the  differential  in 
2:43:2899:14:14:72:546:420:12:Times:12:Times:F:proximity to  Superfund  sites  among  African  American  mothers.  These  results  have  important 
2:44:2998:14:14:72:545:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:implications   for studies   of   “neighborhood   effects”   and   confirm   an   important   mechanism 
2:45:3101:14:14:72:546:392:12:Times:12:Times:F:underlying  observed  correlations between  race  and  pollution  in  the  environmental  justice 
2:46:3198:14:14:72:545:378:12:Times:12:Times:F:literature.  Our  results  also  suggest  that  the basic  utility  maximization  assumptions  underlying 
2:47:3303:14:14:72:546:364:12:Times:12:Times:F:hedonic and residential sorting models may often be violated, resulting in an important distortion 
2:48:3401:14:42:72:254:350:12:Times:12:Times:F:in the provision of local public goods.
2:49:3440:42:14:72:156:308:12:Times:12:Times:F:Peter Christensen
2:50:3457:14:14:72:173:294:12:Times:12:Times:F:University of Illinois
2:51:3479:14:14:72:163:280:12:Times:12:Times:F:431 Mumford Hall
2:52:3495:14:14:72:156:266:12:Times:12:Times:F:1301 W. Gregory
2:53:3510:14:14:72:180:252:12:Times:12:Times:F:Urbana, Illinois 61801
2:54:3532:14:28:72:169:238:12:Times:12:Times:F:pchrist@illinois.edu
2:55:3552:28:14:72:175:210:12:Times:12:Times:F:Christopher Timmins
2:56:3571:14:14:72:198:196:12:Times:12:Times:F:Department of Economics
2:57:3594:14:14:72:152:182:12:Times:12:Times:F:Duke University
2:58:3609:14:14:72:213:168:12:Times:12:Times:F:209 Social Sciences Building
2:59:3637:14:14:72:149:154:12:Times:12:Times:F:P.O. Box 90097
2:60:3651:14:14:72:195:140:12:Times:12:Times:F:Durham, NC 27708-0097
2:61:3672:14:14:72:124:126:12:Times:12:Times:F:and NBER
2:62:3680:14:0:72:223:112:12:Times:12:Times:F:christopher.timmins@duke.edu
3:63:3708:0:33:99:222:702:246:g_d0_f2:246:g_d0_f2:C:1  Introduction
3:64:3723:33:21:99:510:669:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The choice of residential location is a critical economic decision for households in the
3:65:3811:21:22:99:510:648:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:United States.  It a↵ects the neighborhood with which one interacts on a daily basis.
3:66:3896:22:22:99:510:626:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:This can have important implications both in the short-run and long-run, and impacts
3:67:3980:22:22:99:510:604:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:can even accumulate across generations. Over the past decade, a growing body of evidence
3:68:4068:22:21:99:521:582:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:has found neighborhood poverty (Kling et al.,2007), employment (Bayer et al.,2008  ),
3:69:4153:21:22:99:511:561:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:school quality (Chetty et al.,2011), violent crime (Kling et al.,2005), and health outcomes
3:70:4244:22:22:99:511:539:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:from pollution exposures (Currie et al.,2015) to be important, elevating concern about
3:71:4330:22:22:99:511:517:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:whether certain groups are systematically excluded from beneficial neighborhood e↵ects
3:72:4416:22:22:99:510:495:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:or disadvantaged by segregation or discriminatory steering. A large body of observational
3:73:4505:22:21:99:510:473:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:research has also documented that patterns of residential sorting are strongly correlated
3:74:4594:21:22:99:510:452:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:with economic disparities and pollution exposures between racial groups in the United
3:75:4679:22:22:99:511:430:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:States (Alexander and Currie, 2017,Currie, 2011,Mohai et al.,2009). It has, however,
3:76:4763:22:22:99:511:408:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:been extremely challenging to disentangle the e↵ect of discrimination (steering) from
3:77:4848:22:22:99:405:386:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:preference-based sorting in evaluating these persistent disparities.
3:78:4916:22:21:115:511:364:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:This paper studies the e↵ect of racial discrimination on residential location choices
3:79:5001:21:22:99:510:343:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in the United States housing market. Specifically, we present experimental evidence on
3:80:5087:22:22:99:510:321:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:discriminatory behavior of real estate agents and housing providers from a nation-wide
3:81:5173:22:22:99:510:299:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:paired-actor study that was conducted by the Urban Institute in conjunction with the
3:82:5257:22:21:99:510:277:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Department of Housing and Urban Development (Turner et al.,2013). The 2012 Housing
3:83:5339:21:22:99:510:256:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Discrimination Study utilized a matched-pair block randomized design that simulates the
3:84:5426:22:22:99:510:234:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:housing search process for a matched pair of “testers” who are assigned attributes that
3:85:5513:22:22:99:510:212:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:make them equally qualified to purchase a particular house or rent a particular unit.
3:86:5598:22:22:99:510:190:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Paired testers are matched to an advertised listing and randomly assigned to a real estate
3:87:5688:22:21:99:511:168:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:agent; di↵erent aspects of their search experience are then documented. According to
3:88:5772:21:22:99:510:147:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:evidence from a series of four studies executed between 1977 and 2012, incidence of the
3:89:5859:22:22:99:510:125:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:most blatant forms of housing discrimination has declined dramatically in the period
3:90:5943:22:0:99:510:103:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:following the Fair Housing Act (FHA) of 1968, but it is less clear that more subtle forms
4:91:6033:0:22:99:259:702:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:of discrimination have also fallen.1
4:92:6069:22:22:115:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:With respect to locational choice, prior studies have described the process of steering
4:93:6156:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:buyers into same-race neighborhoods and exacerbating historical racial segregation in
4:94:6241:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the housing market (Galster and Godfrey,2005  , Yinger,1995). Our paper builds upon
4:95:6324:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:these segregation studies by testing for evidence of systematic di↵erences in key local
4:96:6411:22:22:99:511:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:attributes that have been shown to a↵ect both economic and non-economic outcomes.
4:97:6492:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The HUD study provides detailed information on the price, characteristics, condition,
4:98:6577:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and the exact locations of homes that are shown and recommended to white versus
4:99:6656:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:minority buyers. While discriminatory behavior on the part of real estate agents and
4:100:6740:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:housing providers is just one of several channels through which racial discrimination can
4:101:6829:22:22:99:522:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:constrain housing options of minorities (Aaronson et al.,2017,Zhao et al.,2005  , Ondrich
4:102:6918:22:21:99:511:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:et al.,2003  , 1998  , Yinger,1995), this channel is crucial for disentangling the e↵ect of
4:103:7009:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:illegal discrimination (steering) from preference-based sorting in determining di↵erences
4:104:7098:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in access to local amenities/advantages across racial groups. We formalize this argument
4:105:7186:22:22:99:511:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:by examining the e↵ect of discrimination on location choice using a theoretical model of
4:106:7274:22:22:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:housing search, which motivates the identification of discriminatory behavior in reduced-
4:107:7363:22:21:99:510:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:form tests as well as the welfare implications of a housing search with discrimination
4:108:7449:21:22:99:153:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:constraints.
4:109:7461:22:22:115:511:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Our results indicate that systematic di↵erences in the homes shown to minority ver-
4:110:7544:22:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sus white testers impart a number of critical disadvantages. Minority testers are (relative
4:111:7635:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to their white counterparts) systematically recommended homes in neighborhoods with
4:112:7718:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:higher poverty rates, fewer college educated families, and fewer skilled workers. Important
4:113:7809:22:22:99:510:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:for the analysis of environmental injustice, they are also steered towards neighborhoods
4:114:7897:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:with higher concentrations of Superfund sites and releases from the Toxic Release In-
4:115:7982:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ventory (TRI). These disparities are consistent across specifications, are stronger in the
4:116:8072:22:21:99:510:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:case of African American testers, and become more pronounced when tester pairs signal
4:117:8157:21:23:99:510:136:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:preferences for the neighborhood characteristic in question. In addition, African Amer-
4:118:8244:23:14:100:511:113:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:1Housing discrimination is illegal according to the Fair Housing Act of 1968, which was amended in
4:119:8342:14:11:99:510:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:1988. Blatant forms of discrimination include denial of appointments with a housing provider or refusal
4:120:8445:11:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:to show an advertised house. Less blatant forms include disparities in the number of houses shown or in
4:121:8548:11:0:99:301:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:the condition of the houses that are recommended.
5:122:8598:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ican testers are more likely to be recommended houses in neighborhoods with higher
5:123:8680:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:assault rates and lower percentages of skilled workers. While only statistically signifi-
5:124:8769:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:cant for African Americans with children, all minority groups are also more likely to be
5:125:8857:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:recommended houses in neighborhoods with lower quality schools. We also find that mi-
5:126:8942:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:nority testers are less likely to be recommended houses in white neighborhoods, however,
5:127:9030:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:evidence suggests that segregation-based steering (i.e., directed by neighborhood race)
5:128:9117:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:cannot explain the disparities in pollution exposures resulting from discrimination. We
5:129:9204:21:22:99:511:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:find that di↵erences are magnified for mothers and are large enough to fully account for
5:130:9292:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:higher rates of sorting among African American mothers into homes near Superfund sites,
5:131:9379:22:22:99:521:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:as has been found in previous research on in utero pollution exposures (Currie, 2011  ).
5:132:9467:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, we discuss the implications of discrimination of the sort revealed in this study for
5:133:9560:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:measures of marginal willingness to pay for an important set of local public goods (e.g., to
5:134:9652:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:avoid exposure to air toxics). The distortionary impact of discrimination has important
5:135:9739:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:consequences on the political incentives underlying the provision and allocation of local
5:136:9828:22:22:99:161:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:public goods.
5:137:9841:22:22:115:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:This paper proceeds as follows. Section 2 summarizes a number of relevant literatures,
5:138:9927:22:21:99:510:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:including those that describe experimental approaches for broadly measuring discrimina-
5:139:10014:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tion; the evaluation of housing discrimination studies; “neighborhood e↵ects” and their
5:140:10101:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:e↵ects on long-run outcomes; and hedonics, residential sorting models, and related non-
5:141:10188:22:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:market valuation techniques. Section 3 describes the 2012 Housing Discrimination Study
5:142:10274:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:(HDS), which is the source of our paired tester audit study data. In Section 4, we develop
5:143:10364:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a model of housing search to characterize the welfare e↵ects of discrimination. Section
5:144:10451:22:22:99:510:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:5 describes our data with a particular focus on spatial attribute information that we
5:145:10536:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:connect to the houses in HDS 2012. Section 6 reports results that characterize the ex-
5:146:10622:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tent of discrimination in the space of neighborhood attributes, and discusses some of the
5:147:10711:22:0:99:475:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:potential mechanisms that might be driving discrimination. Section 7 concludes.
6:148:10791:0:38:99:249:702:246:g_d0_f2:246:g_d0_f2:C:2  Prior Literature
6:149:10810:38:29:99:488:664:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:2.1  Experimental Approaches to Measuring Discrimination
6:150:10866:29:21:99:510:635:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:A large and growing literature utilizes field experiment techniques for detecting discrim-
6:151:10956:21:22:99:511:614:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ination.Bertrand and Duflo(2016) summarize this literature, focusing on the di↵erence
6:152:11041:22:22:99:510:592:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:between audit and correspondence studies. Audit studies typically utilize a matched-pair
6:153:11129:22:22:99:511:570:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:randomized design, where a pair of actors or “testers”, di↵ering only in the character-
6:154:11216:22:22:99:510:548:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:istic of interest (e.g., race), is sent into the field to carry out an economic activity. In
6:155:11308:22:21:99:510:526:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a correspondence study, fictitious applicants correspond only by mail or Internet.  In
6:156:11394:21:22:99:510:505:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:partnership with university researchers and institutions, the United States Department
6:157:11480:22:22:99:510:483:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of Housing and Urban Development has conducted four major, multi-city audit studies
6:158:11563:22:22:99:510:461:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:that are designed to measure the incidence of discrimination against African American,
6:159:11649:22:21:99:510:439:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Hispanic, and Asian and Native American minority testers (relative to a white control) in
6:160:11738:21:22:99:510:418:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the context of a rental housing or real estate search. The first such study was conducted
6:161:11827:22:22:99:510:396:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in 1977, with successive iterations occurring in 1989, 2000, and 2012. Audit studies have
6:162:11916:22:22:99:521:374:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:similarly been used to study bargaining at car dealerships (Ayres and Siegelman,1995  ),
6:163:12004:22:22:99:511:352:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:gender discrimination in hiring at restaurants (Neumark et al.,1996), and the combined
6:164:12090:22:21:99:383:330:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:e↵ects of race and criminal record on hiring (Pager, 2003  ).
6:165:12151:21:22:115:510:309:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Audit studies are designed to fully simulate engagements between individuals in a
6:166:12232:22:22:99:510:287:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:market, often involving a series of in-person interactions and involving a full represen-
6:167:12321:22:22:99:510:265:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tation of racial identity.  As a result, they provide a more complete characterization
6:168:12407:22:21:99:510:243:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of discriminatory behavior as it operates in many markets.  However, this also makes
6:169:12491:21:22:99:510:222:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:them much more expensive to implement at powered scales (and therefore less common).
6:170:12575:22:22:99:511:200:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Siegelman and Heckman(1993) andHeckman(1998) describe other limitations of audit
6:171:12655:22:22:99:510:178:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:studies – for instance, it is unlikely that testers will be identical in all respects except for
6:172:12751:22:22:99:510:156:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the attribute of interest. Moreover, testers are aware of their role and may act in such a
6:173:12841:22:21:99:510:134:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:way as to try to sway the results towards or against finding evidence of discrimination.
6:174:12929:21:0:99:510:113:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The investigator retains more control in a correspondence study, as testers do not actually
7:175:13021:0:42:99:407:702:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:exist and their attributes can therefore be more easily controlled.2
7:176:13089:42:29:99:379:660:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:2.2  Discrimination in the Housing Market
7:177:13130:29:22:99:510:631:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Within the economics literature, HDS audits have been utilized to study the persistence of
7:178:13220:22:22:99:510:609:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:discrimination and underlying behavioral mechanisms such as animus-based versus statis-
7:179:13307:22:21:99:510:587:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tical discrimination (Guryan and Charles,2013  , Dymski,2006).3An additional hypothe-
7:180:13392:21:22:99:510:566:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sis posits that real estate agents may have an incentive to discriminate against people of
7:181:13482:22:22:99:510:544:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:color in order to avoid losing a prejudiced white customer base. Under this hypothesis,
7:182:13569:22:22:99:511:522:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Yinger(1995) suggests that real estate agents will discriminate more in neighborhoods
7:183:13654:22:22:99:510:500:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:that are at risk of being ”flipped”and or disproportionately against minority families with
7:184:13745:22:21:99:470:478:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:children if their white customers are particularly sensitive to school integration.
7:185:13828:21:22:115:510:457:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:The consistency of the HUD design (especially 1989, 2000, 2012) has allowed for
7:186:13907:22:22:99:510:435:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:comparisons of discriminatory behavior over time, with results generally indicating a
7:187:13992:22:22:99:521:413:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:decline in exlusionary practices over the past five decades (Turner et al.,2013,2002  ).
7:188:14080:22:21:99:510:391:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Using data from a paired-tester audit study in Boston in 1981 that considered white and
7:189:14167:21:22:99:511:370:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:black renters,Yinger(1986) finds that black renters are informed about 30% fewer rental
7:190:14254:22:22:99:510:348:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:units than their white counterpart, who is also invited to inspect 57% more apartments.4
7:191:14342:22:22:99:511:326:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Page(1995) builds upon this study by employing a Poisson model to describe the number
7:192:14427:22:22:99:510:304:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of houses shown. Using HDS 1989, she finds that black and Hispanic testers are shown
7:193:14511:22:21:99:510:282:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:80% to 90%, respectively, of the number of units shown to white testers. Results are
7:194:14595:21:22:99:510:261:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:similar for rental and sales properties and are best explained, for black testers, by the
7:195:14684:22:28:99:510:239:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:white customer or statistical discrimination mechanisms. A series of subsequent papers
7:196:14770:28:14:100:511:211:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:2One problem that might arise in both audit and correspondence studies is the potential for those being
7:197:14873:14:11:99:510:197:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:audited to check the online profile of the tester or fictitious applicant, particularly in markets where there
7:198:14983:11:11:99:510:186:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:is a high return to gathering such information (e.g., high skilled labor). To address this problem in a
7:199:15086:11:11:99:511:175:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:correspondence study,Acquisti and Fong(2015) create an online presence for their fictitious applicants
7:200:15188:11:11:99:510:164:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:in an analysis of discrimination in the labor market. In parallel analyses of labor and rental markets,
7:201:15291:11:7:99:484:153:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:Bartoˇs et al.(2013) create websites for applicants and keep track of how often they are accessed.
7:202:15389:7:14:100:511:146:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:3The common theme in these papers is measuring discrimination at the initial point of contact when
7:203:15487:14:11:99:510:132:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:the real estate agent recommends rental units or homes for purchase, and when customers are invited to
7:204:15589:11:11:99:510:121:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:inspect a property. Studies di↵er in the measures of discrimination they use and in the minority groups
7:205:15692:11:8:99:154:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:they consider.
7:206:15706:8:14:100:511:102:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:4Yinger argues for the inclusion of tester-pair fixed e↵ects to control for unobservables that are common
7:207:15811:14:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:to a particular audit experiment (i.e., o-ce conditions on the day that the two testers visited a particular
7:208:15919:11:0:99:403:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:real estate agent), and these have henceforth been common in the literature.
8:209:15996:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:find similar evidence of predjudice among real estate agents, statistical discrimination,
8:210:16085:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and catering to a white customer base (Ondrich et al.,1998,2003,Zhao et al.,2005). The
8:211:16171:22:21:99:511:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:latter two papers introduce the fixed-e↵ects logit model, controlling for trial fixed e↵ects
8:212:16263:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:while looking for evidence of discrete instances of discrimination, and controls for testers’
8:213:16356:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f9:119:g_d0_f3:B:actualcharacteristics, recognizing that some elements of these might show through during
8:214:16444:22:22:99:145:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the audit.
8:215:16454:22:21:115:511:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Yinger(1997) builds on the analysis ofCourant(1978) to develop a model of housing
8:216:16535:21:22:99:511:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:search, where discrimination a↵ects the surplus homebuyers receive through five separate
8:217:16623:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mechanisms: (1) the number of houses shown, (2) the amount of assistance and encour-
8:218:16707:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:agement received, (3) assistance in the loan application process, (4) loan approval, and
8:219:16795:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:(5) physical moving costs. Calibrating the model, he finds that these mechanisms collec-
8:220:16883:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tively result in a $4,000 lower expected surplus for black homebuyers from the housing
8:221:16969:21:22:99:511:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:search process.5Since the HDS research design focuses on discrimination that occurs at
8:222:17055:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the point of initial contact with the real estate agent – i.e., the point at which recommen-
8:223:17147:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:dations are given and the choice set is narrowed – the results of HDS analyses describe
8:224:17234:22:21:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:one particular form of housing market discrimination that could be compounded by other
8:225:17320:21:22:99:511:354:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:forms of discrimination in the process of searching for, financing6, and purchasing a home.
8:226:17411:22:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Prior literature has included arguments in favor of and against the reliable extension of
8:227:17500:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:inferences from partial audit studies to estimate the full extent of compounded impacts,
8:228:17588:22:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:though it is clear that the direct results of the HDS must be interpreted as a lower bound.
8:229:17679:22:21:115:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:According to the comparative work done across HDS studies, the single persistent
8:230:17759:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:form of discrimination in the housing market is “discriminatory steering” of minority
8:231:17844:22:22:99:511:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:testers into minority neighborhoods (Dymski,2006  , Galster and Godfrey,2005,Yinger,
8:232:17928:22:33:99:521:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:1995  ). These studies provide important motivation for research on the characteristics of
8:233:18018:33:15:100:511:168:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:5Yinger(1997) does not account for di↵erences in the attributes of houses or neighborhoods shown to
8:234:18117:15:7:99:198:153:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:African American testers
8:235:18141:7:14:100:511:146:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:6There is a large body of evidence that documents the presence of discrimination in mortgage and other
8:236:18243:14:11:99:511:132:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:lending markets (Dymski,2006). It is possible (indeed likely, based on prior evidence) that discrimination
8:237:18349:11:11:99:510:121:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:also occurs in the mortgage lending industry. O-cial government guidance for mortgage lenders in the
8:238:18449:11:11:99:510:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:1930’s suggested that neighborhoods with a high percentage of people of color constituted risky loans,
8:239:18551:11:11:99:511:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:drawing a red line around those areas and steering funds away (Aaronson et al.,2017). If minority home
8:240:18653:11:11:99:511:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:buyers were steered towards those neighborhoods, red-lining would make home-ownership more di-cult,
8:241:18752:11:0:99:205:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:or at least more expensive.
9:242:18780:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhoods that define buyer/renter choice sets, though the prior work has emphasized
9:243:18868:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the role of discrimination in perpetuating segregation rather than the intersection between
9:244:18959:22:42:99:329:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:discriminatory steering and neighborhood e↵ects.
9:245:19007:42:29:99:272:616:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:2.3  Neighborhood E↵ects
9:246:19031:29:21:99:510:587:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:If housing market discrimination alters an individual’s choice set and ultimately influences
9:247:19123:21:22:99:510:566:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhood choice, then a growing body of evidence on neighborhood e↵ects indicates
9:248:19208:22:22:99:510:544:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:that it could have impacts on labor market outcomes, educational attainment, criminal
9:249:19293:22:22:99:510:522:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:activity, physical safety and environmental health. Much of the experimental evidence
9:250:19378:22:22:99:511:500:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:on neighborhood e↵ects has come from the from the ”Moving to Opportunity” (MTO)
9:251:19457:22:21:99:510:478:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:program, which provided housing vouchers to public housing residents that could be used
9:252:19544:21:22:99:511:457:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to secure a residence in a neighborhood with a lower than 10% poverty rate.7MTO
9:253:19623:22:22:99:510:435:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:has demonstrated that the the poverty level of a neighborhood is a key determinant of
9:254:19708:22:22:99:510:413:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:long-run outcomes – poverty levels likely capture a set of mechanisms underlying human
9:255:19794:22:21:99:510:391:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:capital formation, such as levels of crime and public safety, the quality of schools, pollution
9:256:19889:21:22:99:389:370:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:exposures, and other types of spillovers within neighborhoods.
9:257:19951:22:22:115:511:348:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:In an intent to treat analysis,Kling et al.(2005) find that female youth are less likely
9:258:20039:22:22:99:510:326:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to commit violent or property crimes with MTO treatment assignment.  Incidence of
9:259:20120:22:22:99:510:304:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:participation in violent crime also falls for males assigned MTO treatment, but after a
9:260:20207:22:21:99:510:282:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:short-term drop, property crime rises again for this group. Other papers have focused
9:261:20292:21:22:99:511:261:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:on other health and economic outcomes.Sanbonmatsu et al.(2006) look four to seven
9:262:20373:22:22:99:510:239:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:years after the MTO treatment and find little to no evidence of impacts on test scores
9:263:20459:22:22:99:511:217:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:for children treated by MTO.Kling et al.(2007) similarly find little evidence of impacts
9:264:20547:22:21:99:510:195:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:on physical health or economic outcomes of adults.  They do, however, find evidence
9:265:20630:21:22:99:510:174:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of strong mental health benefits for adults and female youth.  These e↵ects are o↵set
9:266:20715:22:22:99:510:152:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:by adverse e↵ects on male youth.Ludwig et al.(2013) take a longer view (i.e., 10-15
9:267:20798:22:22:99:510:130:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:years after the MTO treatment) and find no evidence of improvements in adult economic
9:268:20883:22:17:99:510:108:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:outcomes, but large improvements in some health outcomes (e.g., incidence of obesity
9:269:20967:17:14:100:511:91:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:7A second treatment group was randomized to receive a Section 8 voucher with no constraints on use
9:270:21065:14:0:99:377:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:and a third treatment group simply retained access to public housing.
10:271:21135:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and diabetes). Focusing on outcomes for children, they find no evidence of impacts on
10:272:21220:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:educational attainment, but do find some health benefits for girls. The program appears,
10:273:21308:22:21:99:363:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:however, to have been detrimental to the health of boys.
10:274:21364:21:22:115:511:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Other research has focused on the duration of time spent in di↵erent types of neigh-
10:275:21448:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:borhoods.Clampet-Lundquist and Massey(2008) find evidence that time spent in
10:276:21524:22:22:99:511:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:high poverty neighborhoods a↵ects economic self-su-ciency (i.e., earnings, employment,
10:277:21610:22:21:99:511:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:TANF, and food stamps). More recently,Chetty et al.(2016) analyzed the age at which
10:278:21693:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a child experiences a switch in neighborhood attributes with MTO, finding that the du-
10:279:21779:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ration of exposure to a low poverty neighborhood plays an important role in the size of
10:280:21866:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the beneficial e↵ect, which o↵sets the negative impacts of “disruption”. Specifically, those
10:281:21958:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:who are randomly assigned to the experimental voucher prior to age 13 experienced a
10:282:22041:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:31% increase in income in their mid-20’s relative to a control group; those assigned after
10:283:22131:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:age 13 experienced an insignificant drop relative to the control, suggesting that benefits
10:284:22221:22:22:99:359:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:accrued were insu-cient to cover the costs of the move.
10:285:22276:22:22:115:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:There is a mostly separate body of evidence demonstrating that neighborhood pollu-
10:286:22358:22:22:99:511:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tion exposures have substantial impacts on health outcomes.Currie and Neidell(2005)
10:287:22441:22:21:99:511:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:find that pollution levels from nearby toxic plants have important e↵ects on infant health,
10:288:22532:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:which correspond to a 3% increase in the incidence of low birthweight within 1 mile of
10:289:22618:22:22:99:511:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a plant.8In utero exposure to pollution from nearby tra-c congestion also substantially
10:290:22705:22:22:99:522:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a↵ects birthweight (Currie and Walker,2011  ). A separate study finds that carbon monox-
10:291:22793:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ide has a strong e↵ect on the infant mortality rate in California, with the drop observed
10:292:22882:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:over the course of the 1990’s estimated to have saved 991 infant lives (Currie and Neidell,
10:293:22973:22:22:99:521:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:2005  ). Using the universe of health records of children born in New Jersey between 2006
10:294:23062:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and 2010,Alexander and Currie(2017) find that the two-fold di↵erential in asthma rates
10:295:23148:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:between African American and other racial groups disappears when the sample is split
10:296:23232:22:33:99:469:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to examine di↵erences within our outside majority African American zip codes.
10:297:23309:33:14:100:510:124:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:8In prior research at the county level,Currie and Schmieder(2009) demonstrate that fugitive emissions
10:298:23410:14:11:99:510:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:of toxic pollutants such as cadmium and toluene have important impacts on infant birthweight. Using
10:299:23509:11:11:99:511:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:a twin study,Black et al.(2007) find that a 7.5 percent increase in birth weight results in a 1.8 percent
10:300:23614:11:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:increase in earnings among men and a 1 percentage point increase in high school completion among
10:301:23710:11:0:99:129:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:women.
11:302:23717:0:22:115:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:A more recent literature has exploited long-run panel data to more directly examine
11:303:23800:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the impact of exposure to environmental nuisances while in utero on long-run economic
11:304:23885:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:outcomes. In a county-level study,Chay and Greenstone(2003) show that a 1% reduc-
11:305:23966:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tion in exposures to Total Suspended Particulates during the recession of the 1980-1981
11:306:24053:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:resulted in a 0.35% e↵ect in infant mortality.Sanders(2012) utilizes the same natu-
11:307:24136:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ral experiment to measure the e↵ect of pre-natal TSP exposure on long-run educational
11:308:24221:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:outcomes, finding that a one standard deviation decrease in particulate matter exposure
11:309:24308:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:results in a reduction in high school test scores equal to 2% of a standard deviation.
11:310:24394:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Instrumenting for changes in pollution using county-level changes in manufacturing em-
11:311:24480:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ployment, that number rises to 6%.9In a cohort study in Florida,Persico et al.(2016)
11:312:24564:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:find that children conceived to mothers living within close proximity (within 2 miles) of
11:313:24653:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:an untreated Superfund site are more likely to repeat a grade (+7.4 pp), to be suspended
11:314:24741:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:from school (6.6 pp), and have lower test scores (-0.06 std dev) than siblings who were
11:315:24828:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:conceived after clean-up. Children conceived to mothers living at closer proximity (within
11:316:24918:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:1 mile) are 10 percentage points more likely to be diagnosed with a cognitive disability.
11:317:25007:22:21:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Barreca et al.(2017) looks at the long-run impacts of exposure toSO2with variation
11:318:25089:21:22:99:510:354:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:induced by the US Acid Rain Program and proximity to regulated plants. Strong impacts
11:319:25174:22:22:99:508:332:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:on mortality are found, and causal mechanisms are supported by cause of death data.10
11:320:25259:22:22:115:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:There is an active discussion about the impact of neighborhood e↵ects on labor market
11:321:25344:22:22:99:511:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:outcomes and earnings.Chetty et al.(2011) examines the impacts at age 27 of random
11:322:25426:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:assignment to classrooms for 11,571 K-3 students and their teachers in Tennessee. More
11:323:25512:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:experienced kindergarten teachers and better test scores of peers both increase earnings.
11:324:25601:22:22:99:511:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:In addition to the direct e↵ects of disparities in the allocation of public goods (e.g., school
11:325:25696:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:quality, pollution abatement, public safety), empirical evidence suggests that spillovers,
11:326:25786:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:interactions and other positive/negative externalities can also have important neighbor-
11:327:25874:22:21:99:510:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:hood e↵ects. Controlling for sorting,Bayer et al.(2008) find evidence that similar indi-
11:328:25962:21:23:99:510:136:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:viduals living in the same census block are also more likely to work in the same census
11:329:26049:23:14:100:511:113:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:9Local exposure to PM2.5 has been shown to have large e↵ects on the contemporaneous productivity in
11:330:26148:14:8:99:249:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:outdoor workers (Chang et al., 2016).
11:331:26185:8:14:96:511:91:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:10Barreca(2010) analyzes the e↵ect of exposure to malaria while in utero on lifetime education attainment
11:332:26290:14:0:99:191:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:and adult poverty rate.
12:333:26315:0:22:99:511:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:block, suggesting a strong neighborhood referral e↵ect. Good matches lead to more hours
12:334:26402:22:42:99:230:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:worked and higher earnings.
12:335:26429:42:29:99:446:638:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:2.4  Sorting and the Provision of Local Public Goods
12:336:26481:29:22:99:511:609:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:It may be that disparities in neighborhood e↵ects observed between race groups result
12:337:26566:22:21:99:511:587:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:from the locational choices of households.  For instance,Currie(2011) provides some
12:338:26649:21:22:99:510:566:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:evidence that the mothers who are most likely to live within the vicinity of a Superfund
12:339:26737:22:22:99:510:544:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:site after cleanup are more likely to be white and college educated.  Similarly, white
12:340:26823:22:22:99:510:522:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mothers are less likely to reside within the vicinity of a plant that emits toxic pollutants
12:341:26915:22:22:99:511:500:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:after emissions are disclosed. While these estimates suggest di↵erential patterns of sorting
12:342:27007:22:21:99:510:478:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in response to changes in the level or information about pollution exposures, it is not clear
12:343:27100:21:22:99:510:457:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:whether all households in these samples had access to the same choices. The hedonics and
12:344:27188:22:22:99:510:435:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sorting literatures have typically ignored housing market discrimination because it cannot
12:345:27278:22:22:99:510:413:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:be identified from observational data in housing markets. However, if discrimination is at
12:346:27368:22:21:99:510:391:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:play, then we cannot expect all housing units to be freely chosen. This distortion would
12:347:27456:21:22:99:511:370:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:bias estimates of the value of di↵erent amenities. In the simplest terms, we may understate
12:348:27547:22:22:99:510:348:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a minority group’s willingness to pay for pollution reductions if those households live in
12:349:27637:22:22:99:443:326:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a polluted neighborhood not by free choice but because of discrimination.
12:350:27710:22:22:115:510:304:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:The most commonly used methods for valuing local public goods and amenities rely on
12:351:27793:22:21:99:511:282:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the observed decisions that individuals make in housing markets.Rosen(1974) provides
12:352:27877:21:22:99:510:261:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the theory for recovering preferences from residential location decisions.  Simply put,
12:353:27964:22:22:99:510:239:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the hedonic gradient reveals the slope of the individual’s utility function in the space
12:354:28052:22:22:99:510:217:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of amenities and house prices. That slope represents marginal willingness to pay under
12:355:28138:22:22:99:510:195:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the assumption that individuals are free to choose where to live (i.e., decisions were
12:356:28224:22:21:99:510:173:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:not constrained by discrimination).  This same assumption is required for a class of
12:357:28308:21:22:99:511:152:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:models of e-cient public goods provision beginning withTiebout(1956).  While the
12:358:28388:22:22:99:510:130:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:hedonic literature uses the equilibrium outcome of those sorting decisions, a structural
12:359:28476:22:22:99:510:108:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:literature builds models that instead derive preference estimates from the sorting decisions
12:360:28568:22:0:99:510:86:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:themselves. Sorting models have also been used to predict the outcomes of urban policies,
13:361:28659:0:22:99:511:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:especially when those policies are large and likely to result in equilibrium feedback e↵ects.
13:362:28752:22:22:99:511:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Reviews of the hedonics and sorting literatures are now available. SeeChamp et al.(2003)
13:363:28840:22:21:99:511:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:or Palmquist(2005) for a review of the hedonics literature, and the survey of the sorting
13:364:28929:21:50:99:266:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:literature inKumino↵et al.(2013).
13:365:28962:50:32:99:400:587:246:g_d0_f2:246:g_d0_f2:C:3  2012 Housing Discrimination Study
13:366:28998:32:22:99:510:555:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The 2012 Housing Discrimination Study was conducted in 28 metropolitan areas, with
13:367:29080:22:22:99:510:533:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sampling designed to represent the racial/ethnic composition of the national housing
13:368:29164:22:22:99:510:511:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:market based on the geographic distribution of each minority group as documented in
13:369:29247:22:21:99:510:489:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the 2010 US population census. The 2012 HDS utilized a matched-pair block randomized
13:370:29331:21:22:99:510:468:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:design, where recruitment and assignment was conducted in each of the 28 metropolitan
13:371:29416:22:22:99:510:446:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:area field o-ces. Testers were blind matched to a partner based on their age and gender.
13:372:29504:22:22:99:510:424:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:They were both then provided with a profile of characteristics to use throughout the
13:373:29588:22:22:99:510:402:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:study: income, assets, debt levels, family circumstances, job characteristics, education
13:374:29676:22:21:99:510:380:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:levels, and housing preferences. The design involves randomly sampling the distribution
13:375:29763:21:22:99:510:359:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of rental and real estate advertisements available for the market at the time of the study.
13:376:29854:22:22:99:511:337:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Upon each draw of a listing and corresponding local real estate o-ce or rental housing
13:377:29940:22:22:99:510:315:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:provider, a pair of testers is randomly assigned and undergoes a housing search process.11
13:378:30030:22:21:99:510:293:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Income, asset and debt levels are assigned to make testers unambiguously well-qualified for
13:379:30121:21:22:99:510:272:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the advertised listing.12Housing preferences and family/job characteristics are assigned
13:380:30209:22:137:99:331:250:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to match the characteristics of the advertisement.
13:381:30259:137:14:96:511:113:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:11Testers meet independently with a local test coordinator to review test protocols and receive an assigned
13:382:30366:14:8:99:151:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:listing/o-ce.
13:383:30379:8:14:96:511:91:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:122012 HDS documentation states that the assignment of qualifications errs on the side of making minority
13:384:30484:14:0:99:461:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:testers were slightly better qualified than their white counterparts for an advertised listing.
