19:585:40296:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mended houses. In Los Angeles, 5 out of 23 total recommendations are shared between
19:586:40379:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the two testers. However, this is not always the case – the white and Asian tester only
19:587:40466:22:21:99:494:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:share one common recommendation out of 15 total recommended houses in Chicago.
19:588:40544:21:22:115:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:The full sample of properties from the buyer study contains 6,962 advertised listings
19:589:40629:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and 21,496 recommendations. Basic characteristics and price information are taken from
19:590:40715:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the HUD study data files. The HUD data files also contain extensive data on the true and
19:591:40803:22:22:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:assigned characteristics of testers, the timing and sequence of appointments, characteris-
19:592:40893:22:21:99:510:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tics of the agents and representatives, and the quality of interactions between testers and
19:593:40984:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:agents during the study. Table1 reports descriptive statistics on the general characteris-
19:594:41074:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tics of testers recruited into in the sample. The average age of testers in the study is 41
19:595:41165:22:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and about two thirds of them are female. Home-owners and renters are well-represented
19:596:41250:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:amongst those working as testers, though the majority are renters at the time of their
19:597:41336:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:participation in the study. The median tester in the sample has a bachelor’s degree and
19:598:41423:22:42:99:480:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:more than half of the sample earns less than $30,000 per year in personal income.
19:599:41504:42:29:99:253:181:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:5.2  Data on Outcomes
19:600:41525:29:22:99:510:152:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:We geocode the addresses of advertised and recommended homes reported in the 2012
19:601:41606:22:22:99:510:130:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:HDS and merge them with contemporaneous data at the census block group level from
19:602:41687:22:22:99:510:108:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the American Community Survey (ACS). The 2008-2012 5-year moving average ACS
19:603:41763:22:0:99:510:86:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:provides data on the share of white, African American, Asian, and Hispanic households
20:604:41850:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:at the census block group level. We also obtain ACS data on the share of households at
20:605:41936:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:or below the poverty line, the share of households with at least one member with a college
20:606:42026:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:degree, and the share of households with at least one member who is employed in a high
20:607:42112:21:22:99:492:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:skilled occupation (defined as management, business, science, and arts occupations).
20:608:42196:22:22:115:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Advertised and recommended homes are also merged with information about local
20:609:42273:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:pollution exposures/sources from monitoring programs conducted by the US Environ-
20:610:42354:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mental Protection Agency (EPA). For each home in the sample, we create measures of:
20:611:42437:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:(1) the number of Superfund sites within a 5km radius using the exact location and extent
20:612:42526:22:22:99:511:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of sites throughout the United States,20(2) the risk of exposure (in 2012) to industrial
20:613:42614:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:chemical releases from facilities monitored by the EPA’s Toxics Release Inventory,21and
20:614:42701:22:22:99:444:484:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:(3) particulate matter (PM2.5) concentrations taken from satellite data.22
20:615:42775:22:21:115:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, we merge information about crime (count of violent assaults)23and school
20:616:42856:21:22:99:511:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:quality (“GreatSchools” ratings)24that are scraped from the platform of a major online
20:617:42942:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:realty service. Data were scraped for each property using the addresses of houses listed in
20:618:43033:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the HUD study and both measures relate to the property-level characteristic of the home.
20:619:43121:22:21:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The GreatSchool rating measures the quality of the school that a home is districted for
20:620:43208:21:22:99:510:354:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:or, in cases of no location-based assignment, takes the average of nearby schools. Data
20:621:43295:22:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:collection for these variables was conducted in December 2017 and measures relate to
20:622:43379:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the time of collection. Neighborhood and district-level data for 2012 were not available
20:623:43467:22:22:99:511:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:for HDS markets.  Di↵erences in these outcomes therefore reflect school ratings and
20:624:43550:22:44:99:447:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhood assault counts 5 years after a housing search was conducted.
20:625:43623:44:14:96:511:222:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:20The   exact   location   and   extent   of   Superfund   sites   is   identified   using   data   pro-
20:626:43727:14:11:99:510:208:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:cessed  by  the  Socioeconomic  Data  and  Applications  Center  at  Columbia  University:
20:627:43817:11:8:99:386:197:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:http://sedac.ciesin.columbia.edu/data/collection/superfund/sets/browse
20:628:43887:8:11:96:474:189:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:21https://www.epa.gov/sites/production/files/2018-01/documents/rseimethodologyv2.3.6.pdf
20:629:43975:11:14:96:511:178:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:22PM2.5 can be an important factor in mortality from cardiovascular and respiratory diseases. Satellite
20:630:44078:14:11:99:510:164:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:data are taken from Van Donkelaar et al. (2016), who use Aerosol Optical Depth (AOD) retrievals from
20:631:44178:11:11:99:510:153:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:the NASA MODIS, MISR, and SeaWiFS to recover ground-level PM2.5 concentration. Data have a grid
20:632:44273:11:7:99:214:142:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:cell resolution of 0.01 degree.
20:633:44304:7:14:96:511:135:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:23Assault counts are drawn from multiple sources, including CrimeReports.com, EveryBlock.com and
20:634:44400:14:8:99:163:121:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:SpotCrime.com.
20:635:44414:8:14:96:511:113:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:24GreatSchools  is  a  private  ratings  service  that  combines  information  on  test  scores,  student
20:636:44519:14:11:99:511:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:progress,  and “other factors that make a big di↵erence in how children experience school” to
20:637:44612:11:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:generate a score on a 1-10 scale.   Details on the GreatSchools rating system can be found at
20:638:44705:11:0:99:510:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:https://www.greatschools.org/gk/ratings. District boundaries are provided by Boundaries by Maponics.
21:639:44807:0:29:99:251:702:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:5.3  Advertised Homes
21:640:44828:29:22:99:510:673:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Table2 reports characteristics of the advertised listings that are assigned to testers as
21:641:44917:22:21:99:510:651:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:part of the study. These advertised listings are presented to real estate agents to initiate
21:642:45009:21:22:99:510:630:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a search in the first stage of a trial. They are not representative of the set of all homes.
21:643:45101:22:22:99:510:608:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:More than 70% of the listings assigned to testers are single-family homes. The remaining
21:644:45189:22:22:99:510:586:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:listings are primarily for town-homes (13%) and some multi-family buildings (10.4%).
21:645:45273:22:21:99:510:564:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The average list price of advertised homes in the sample is just over $300,000.  The
21:646:45357:21:22:99:510:543:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:racial composition of the census block group of an advertised listing has, on average, 67%
21:647:45447:22:22:99:510:521:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:White, 9% African American, 7% Asian, and 15% Hispanic (and 2% other). On average,
21:648:45529:22:22:99:510:499:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:advertised listings are in neighborhoods where 9% of the households have incomes at or
21:649:45615:22:22:99:510:477:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:below the poverty line, 50% have at least one member with a college degree, and 47%
21:650:45698:22:42:99:302:455:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:have a member that is in a high skilled job.
21:651:45742:42:29:99:221:413:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:5.4  Balance Tests
21:652:45760:29:21:99:511:384:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Tables3 and4 report the results of balance tests for within-tester pairs, including (1)
21:653:45847:21:22:99:510:363:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:true characteristics of testers (i.e., actor characteristics), (2) characteristics assigned to
21:654:45941:22:22:99:510:341:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:testers, and (3) characteristics of advertised homes. Tests for balance suggest that paired
21:655:46032:22:22:99:510:319:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:actors are not perfectly equivalent in all real-life dimensions, but do not reveal strongly
21:656:46123:22:22:99:511:297:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:significant di↵erences in characteristics.  African American actors have a lower likeli-
21:657:46211:22:21:99:510:275:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:hood of being homeowners than their white tester counterpart (15% lower, significant at
21:658:46298:21:22:99:511:254:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:p<10%). The number of African American testers with personal incomes in the $20,000-
21:659:46382:22:22:99:510:232:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:29,999 range is lower than their white counterparts (21% lower, significant at p<5%), but
21:660:46471:22:22:99:510:210:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:is higher in both the $10,000-19,999 and the $30,000-39,999 ranges. Similar di↵erences
21:661:46557:22:22:99:510:188:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in bin matching are also present for other groups. Hispanic actors tend to have a lower
21:662:46644:22:21:99:511:166:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:probability of having a bachelor’s degree (25% lower, significant at p<10%), but a higher
21:663:46733:21:22:99:510:145:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:probability of having an associate’s or a graduate/professional degree (non-significant).
21:664:46822:22:22:99:510:123:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Asian actors are more likely than their counterparts to have a high school diploma (12%
21:665:46909:22:22:99:240:101:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:higher, significant at p<10%).
21:666:46939:22:0:115:510:79:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:The HUD design intentionally constructs assignment profiles that err on the side
22:667:47021:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of providing minority testers with slightly higher qualifications. For example, minority
22:668:47109:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:testers in all groups have been employed for 1-2 years longer and have lived for 1-2 years
22:669:47199:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:longer at their current address than their white counterparts.  All actor and assigned
22:670:47285:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics are included as controls in the tests for discrimination.  Balance tests
22:671:47373:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:reveal that advertisements for single-family homes are assigned at slightly higher rates
22:672:47461:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and multi-family advertisements at slightly lower rates to Asian testers.  There is no
22:673:47547:22:21:99:511:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:evidence of di↵erences in the pollution levels, block group characteristics, or listing prices
22:674:47641:21:50:99:274:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of homes assigned within tester pairs.
22:675:47679:50:32:99:182:500:246:g_d0_f2:246:g_d0_f2:C:6  Results
22:676:47689:32:22:99:510:468:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:This section reports the results of a series of tests of hypotheses that arise from the model
22:677:47782:22:22:99:510:446:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:presented above. Specifically, we test for e↵ects of the tester’s race on choice set size and
22:678:47875:22:22:99:510:424:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:composition while also exploring the role of the information provided by the tester in the
22:679:47965:22:42:99:235:402:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:form of the advertised house.
22:680:47994:42:29:99:490:360:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:6.1  Are Minority Buyers Given Fewer Choices in a Search?
22:681:48051:29:22:99:510:331:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The model of housing search presented above shows that the expected utility of a buyer’s
22:682:48139:22:21:99:511:309:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:choice set will be unambiguously lower when fewer homes are o↵ered as available choices.
22:683:48227:21:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:A first-order question regarding the e↵ect of housing discrimination concerns the e↵ect of
22:684:48317:22:22:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:real estate agent behavior on the number of recommendations provided to the minority
22:685:48401:22:22:99:274:244:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tester relative to a white counterpart.
22:686:48440:22:22:115:511:222:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Table5 reports estimates from two highly related variants of this test.  A row in
22:687:48521:22:21:99:510:200:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the table presents estimates of di↵erences between a minority tester and a white tester,
22:688:48609:21:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:where minority is defined as self-identified as African American, Hispanic, or Asian. The
22:689:48698:22:22:99:511:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:first two columns test for di↵erences in the total number of recommendations provided
22:690:48783:22:22:99:510:135:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to minority testers relative to the white tester in the same trial, whereas the third and
22:691:48872:22:21:99:511:113:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:fourth columns test for di↵erences in the availability (communicated by the agent) of the
22:692:48961:21:0:99:511:92:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:advertised home. Columns 2 and 4 add controls for di↵erences that may be due to a
23:693:49044:0:22:99:511:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:buyer’s implied preference for price (↵i) and neighborhood characteristics (-i) using the
23:694:49133:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:listing price and racial composition of the neighborhood where the advertised listing is
23:695:49221:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:located. While point estimates indicate that African American and, to a lesser extent,
23:696:49307:21:22:99:511:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Asian buyers receive fewer recommendations than their white counterparts, this di↵erence
23:697:49395:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:is not statistically significant. Neither are any of the di↵erences in the likelihood of the
23:698:49487:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:advertised home being available statistically significant. This is important, as refusing to
23:699:49579:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:suggest a property or making a claim that a particular property is unavailable is a more
23:700:49667:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:blatant form of discrimination that had been prevalent in previous HDS studies. While
23:701:49752:22:22:99:511:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:di↵erences may still persist, they are not statistically significant in this sample.  This
23:702:49842:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:test does not, however, imply anything about di↵erences in thequalityof the houses or
23:703:49927:22:42:99:306:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhoods that are being recommended.
23:704:49968:42:29:99:511:442:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:6.2  Are Minority Buyers Steered into Minority Neighborhoods?
23:705:50029:29:22:99:510:413:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:We begin our discussion of steering by examining the channel that has been the focus of
23:706:50116:22:21:99:511:391:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:previous research (Yinger,1995  , Galster and Godfrey,2005). In particular, we consider
23:707:50203:21:22:99:511:370:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the extent to which the racial composition of neighborhoods di↵ers for homes recom-
23:708:50286:22:22:99:510:348:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mended to minority testers relative to a white counterpart. Table6 reports estimates
23:709:50370:22:22:99:510:326:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of di↵erences in the share of white households in the census block group that contains
23:710:50456:22:22:99:510:304:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a home recommended to a minority versus a white tester.  Columns I - V introduce
23:711:50536:22:21:99:510:282:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:additional controls for attributes of the advertised house, which capture the implied pref-
23:712:50627:21:22:99:511:261:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:erences of the testers for housing price (↵i) and neighborhood characteristics (-i), such
23:713:50716:22:22:99:510:239:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:as neighborhood racial composition and the share of households below the poverty line.
23:714:50802:22:22:99:510:217:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:In each case, African Americans are recommended homes in neighborhoods with a lower
23:715:50885:22:21:99:510:195:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:share of white households compared with those recommended to their white counterparts.
23:716:50971:21:22:99:510:174:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:This di↵erence does not change when we control for the neighborhood racial composition,
23:717:51058:22:28:99:493:152:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:poverty rate, or price of the advertised listing that a tester presents to their agent.25
23:718:51147:28:14:96:510:124:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:25In Appendix Tables16-21, we report results of tests that examine steering into neighborhoods by the
23:719:51248:14:11:99:510:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:share of households from each of the three minority groups in the HDS study. These results demonstrate
23:720:51350:11:11:99:510:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:that African American testers are more likely to be steered towards neighborhoods with a higher share
23:721:51451:11:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:of African American households, but evidence of steering into same-race neighborhoods is not as evident
23:722:51554:11:0:99:181:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:for the other groups.
24:723:51577:0:22:115:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:These estimates confirm the results documented in prior studies on steering and seg-
24:724:51661:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:regation, providing strong evidence that a tester’s race directly influences the racial com-
24:725:51753:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:position of the neighborhoods that define his choice set. This occurs in the absence of
24:726:51840:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:any explicit information about preferences for demographic or other neighborhood char-
24:727:51926:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:acteristics (-i) and is directly attributable to a buyer’s race (Zi).  The e↵ect persists
24:728:52015:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:irrespective of information about neighborhood preferences (-i) implied by an advertised
24:729:52103:22:21:99:235:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:listing presented to an agent.
24:730:52133:21:22:115:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Digging deeper, the estimates presented in Table7 indicate that the results found
24:731:52214:22:22:99:511:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f9:B:in Table6 are primarily driven by steering of African American buyers away fromhigh
24:732:52297:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f9:119:g_d0_f3:B:incomewhite neighborhoods. The steering e↵ect is strong in high income white neigh-
24:733:52380:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:borhoods and is present for the minority group as a whole. It persists when we control
24:734:52466:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:for the listed price, the neighborhood racial composition, and the poverty rate of the
24:735:52552:21:22:99:511:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:advertised listing. These di↵erences become much smaller for African American testers
24:736:52637:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in medium-income white neighborhoods and disappear for the group of minority testers
24:737:52721:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:as a whole. The e↵ect actually reverses for low-income white neighborhoods, such that
24:738:52806:22:22:99:511:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Hispanic and Asian testers aremorelikely than their white counterpart (with the same
24:739:52890:22:42:99:444:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:income) to receive recommendations in a low-income white neighborhood.
24:740:52960:42:29:99:506:311:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:6.3  Are Minorities Disadvantaged by Neighborhood Steering?
24:741:53019:29:21:99:510:282:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:This section presents the core set of tests of our study, which extend the examination
24:742:53105:21:22:99:510:261:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of discriminatory steering to analyze a set of key neighborhood characteristics that have
24:743:53194:22:22:99:511:239:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:been shown to have e↵ects on critical short- and long-run outcomes.  Evidence from
24:744:53276:22:22:99:510:217:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:revealed preference studies in housing markets also indicates that buyers have strong
24:745:53361:22:21:99:510:195:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:preferences for these characteristics.  We therefore assume that the average buyer in
24:746:53446:21:22:99:510:174:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the sample of HUD markets will have preferences for these neighborhood attributes and
24:747:53531:22:22:99:510:152:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:that discriminatory constraints along these dimensions will have a non-trivial impact on
24:748:53619:22:22:99:510:130:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:expected utility. We test for the e↵ect of discriminatory behavior on recommendations
24:749:53704:22:22:99:481:108:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of homes with each of the following neighborhood characteristics described above.
24:750:53785:22:0:115:507:86:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:The two panels of Table8 present core results from tests of di↵erences between the
25:751:53869:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:homes recommended to minority versus white testers along key neighborhood dimensions.
25:752:53954:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:All estimates include controls for characteristics of advertised homes, and for tests that
25:753:54044:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:use census block and pollution variables we report sharpened q-values using a Hochberg
25:754:54130:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:adjustment to control for the family-wise false discovery rate (Benjamini and Hochberg,
25:755:54217:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:1995  ).26We find substantial disparities in the attributes of neighborhoods recommended
25:756:54305:22:22:99:511:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to minority testers relative to their white counterparts. The first panel of Table8 shows
25:757:54394:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:that minority testers (as a whole) are recommended homes in census block groups with
25:758:54478:21:22:99:511:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:higher poverty rates (1.25%) and fewer high skilled neighbors (-2.28%).27Considering the
25:759:54566:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:average values of these neighborhood attributes over all houses in the set of advertised
25:760:54654:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:listings (8.9% and 46.7%), these impacts are substantial (particularly so for poverty).
25:761:54741:22:22:99:511:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:We do not find statistically significant di↵erences in the percentage of college educated
25:762:54830:22:21:99:488:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:residents in neighborhoods recommended to minorities when considered as a whole.
25:763:54910:21:22:115:511:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Below the estimates of di↵erences between white testers and minorities, we report
25:764:54991:22:22:99:511:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:di↵erences by racial group.  Overall, these estimates indicate that African American
25:765:55075:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:testers are shown homes that are in census block groups characterized by higher poverty
25:766:55162:22:22:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:rates (+1.24%), lower shares of skilled workers (-2.72%), and lower shares of college
25:767:55247:22:21:99:510:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:educated neighbors (-3.04%), although the result for poverty is not statistically significant
25:768:55340:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:at traditional levels. The disparities between white and Hispanic testers are even larger
25:769:55429:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in terms of the poverty rate and high-skill neighbors but smaller and insignificant for
25:770:55516:22:22:99:511:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:college share. Di↵erences between white and Asian testers are markedly lower and are
25:771:55600:22:21:99:483:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:not significant along any of the dimensions of neighborhood capital that we study.
25:772:55682:21:22:115:512:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Column 4 of the first panel describes school quality as measured by the“GreatSchools”
25:773:55767:22:22:99:510:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:index.  While the houses recommended to every minority group reflect a lower school
25:774:55850:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:quality than that of the houses recommended to their paired white testers, none of these
25:775:55938:22:22:99:511:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:di↵erences are statistically significant; note, however, that our sample size is approxi-
25:776:56027:22:33:99:511:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mately halved owing to di-culties with merging HUD house addresses with information
25:777:56110:33:14:96:510:124:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:26Hochberg-adjusted p-values are provided for tests of di↵erences between minority and white testers
25:778:56210:14:11:99:511:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:(census block and pollution variables) at the bottom of Table8. Standard test statistics are reported for
25:779:56315:11:8:99:233:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:assault counts and school ratings.
25:780:56349:8:14:96:511:91:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:27High skill is share of census block group employed in American Community Survey defined Management,
25:781:56450:14:0:99:255:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:business, science, and arts occupations.
26:782:56492:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:scraped from the online realty platform. Appendix Table22 demonstrates that, when we
26:783:56576:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:consider tester households separately by the presence of children, the e↵ect school quality
26:784:56667:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:for African American households with kids is indeed negative and significant atp<0.1.
26:785:56752:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:This echos results from previous research which had described real estate agents as being
26:786:56841:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:motivated to discriminate out of a fear of backlash from white customers responding to
26:787:56927:22:22:99:291:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the integration of a neighborhood school.
26:788:56968:22:21:115:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:The second panel of Table8 focuses on neighborhood disamenities – assaults and
26:789:57046:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:three environmental nuisances – proximity to Superfund sites, air toxics (as measured
26:790:57131:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:by the EPA’s RSEI), and PM2.5, an important criteria pollutant with substantial long
26:791:57215:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:run health e↵ects. Considering all minority groups as a whole, we see statistically signif-
26:792:57306:22:22:99:511:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:icant di↵erences in the proximity to Superfund sites and air toxics relative to the houses
26:793:57396:22:21:99:511:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:recommended to white testers. The di↵erence in assaults is positive, although not statis-
26:794:57485:21:22:99:511:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tically significant. However, considering only African Americans, we find the di↵erence
26:795:57572:22:22:99:511:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in assaults to be positive and statistically significant. The magnitude of that di↵erence
26:796:57661:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:(+23.80) is large compared to the average number of assaults across all advertised houses
26:797:57750:22:22:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:(93).  The same is true for Superfund proximity (a di↵erence of +0.12 relative to an
26:798:57834:22:21:99:510:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:average of 0.33) and air toxicity (a di↵erence of +915.45 relative to an average of 6,071).
26:799:57925:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Asians show similar statistically significant di↵erences for Superfund proximity and air
26:800:58013:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:toxics. Point estimates for Hispanics are positive, but estimates are smaller in magnitude
26:801:58103:22:22:99:236:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and statistically insignificant.
26:802:58135:22:21:115:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:In contrast to air toxics, results with respect to particulate matter show very little
26:803:58221:21:22:99:511:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:di↵erence across testers. The average value of particulate matter in the sample of adver-
26:804:58310:22:22:99:511:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tised houses is 9.283. Asian testers do exhibit a statistically significant di↵erence with
26:805:58400:22:22:99:511:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:their white counterparts of -0.1283, but this di↵erence is very small in magnitude. None
26:806:58488:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of the other race groups exhibit statistically significant di↵erences within tester pairs.
26:807:58578:22:21:99:511:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:We suspect that this is due to an important di↵erence between particulate matter and
26:808:58662:21:22:99:510:136:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:air toxics.  In particular, spatial variation in particulate matter concentrations occurs
26:809:58751:22:22:99:510:114:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:over large geographies, whereas air toxics can vary from neighborhood to neighborood.
26:810:58836:22:0:99:510:92:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Because real estate agents do tend to recommend houses within relatively small bu↵ers
27:811:58923:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:around the advertised house to both testers within a pair, the scope for steering with
27:812:59009:22:22:99:468:680:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:respect to particulate matter is far lower than that with respect to air toxics.28
27:813:59091:22:21:115:506:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Table9 reports di↵erences for the subsample of testers (37%) who are assigned an
27:814:59171:21:22:99:511:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:identity of mother (female with children). We find that the di↵erences are magnified for
27:815:59259:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:this group. In particular, we find that minority mothers are steered into neighborhoods
27:816:59346:22:22:99:511:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:with a +4.81% higher poverty rate than white mothers and that this di↵erence is partic-
27:817:59433:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ularly stark for African American (+5.23%) and Hispanic (+5.60%) mothers. Recall that
27:818:59518:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the average poverty rate in the neighborhoods surrounding the set of advertised houses
27:819:59604:22:22:99:511:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:is only 8.9%. Di↵erences in the skill level and share of college educated households in
27:820:59691:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhoods recommended to African American and Hispanic/LatinX mothers are also
27:821:59773:22:22:99:511:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:much larger than the di↵erences for the average tester. Homes recommended to African
27:822:59857:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:American mothers have a 35% higher incidence in nearby assaults (+33), a 52% higher
27:823:59940:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:number of nearby Superfund sites (+0.17), and a 37% higher (+2,269.92) level of expo-
27:824:60025:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sure to air toxics than white mothers. The exception is for elementary school quality – we
27:825:60115:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:find some evidence that homes recommended to Hispanic/LatinX mothers have higher
27:826:60195:22:42:99:214:375:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:school quality (+0.84).29
27:827:60220:42:27:99:465:333:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:6.4  Is there a Single Behavioral Mechanism Underlying
27:828:60274:27:29:133:294:306:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:Discriminatory Steering?
27:829:60298:29:22:99:510:277:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The HDS study was not designed to provide the experimental variation of the sort that
27:830:60383:22:21:99:510:255:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:would be needed to identify behavioral mechanisms underlying discriminatory steering in
27:831:60470:21:22:99:511:234:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the housing market. However, the di↵erences that we identify in discriminatory steering
27:832:60557:22:23:99:510:212:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:do provide valuable information about the behavior of real estate agents. For instance, it
27:833:60647:23:14:96:507:189:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:28Appendix Table24 demonstrates that these di↵erences do not change when we control for the pref-
27:834:60744:14:11:99:510:175:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:erences of di↵erent types of buyers in the study (using preferences implied by the characteristics of
27:835:60845:11:11:99:510:164:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:advertised listings) or for the price of the advertised home. Three columns appear under each neighbor-
27:836:60948:11:11:99:510:153:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:hood characteristic. Moving from the first to the second column adds in controls for the corresponding
27:837:61050:11:10:99:510:142:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:characteristic of the advertised house, the racial composition of the advertised house, and the price of
27:838:61154:10:8:99:501:132:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:the advertised house. In each case, the coe-cient on tester race does not change in a significant way.
27:839:61256:8:14:96:510:124:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:29Appendix Table23 breaks down e↵ects by race and gender. We find similar results with respect to
27:840:61353:14:11:99:510:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:school quality in that e↵ects are large, negative and significant for female African American testers as
27:841:61457:11:11:99:510:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:a whole. We also see that the impact of African American race on the poverty rate of recommended
27:842:61553:11:11:99:511:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:neighborhood is stark for males. Other gender e↵ects are not, however, uniform across all neighborhood
27:843:61655:11:0:99:181:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:attributes and races.
28:844:61678:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:is possible that steering of African Americans away from white neighborhoods is driven by
28:845:61767:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a racial animus and a desire to segregate that population as other studies have posited.
28:846:61855:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:However, a strict interpretation of racial animus is inconsistent with the findings pre-
28:847:61943:21:22:99:511:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sented in Table7, which demonstrate that steering does not occur solely into same-race
28:848:62029:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhoods and but rather depends on the interaction between race and neighborhood
28:849:62114:22:22:99:143:593:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:income.30
28:850:62123:22:21:115:511:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Another explanation that might explain neighborhood e↵ects as well as this income
28:851:62204:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:component could be that real estate agents discriminate by discounting African Amer-
28:852:62288:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ican testers’ financial credentials, steering them towards lower income neighborhoods
28:853:62373:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:where houses are also lower priced. However, as seen in Table10, we do not find any
28:854:62456:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:evidence that minority testers receive recommendations for lower priced homes relative
28:855:62542:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to their white paired testers. Looking at point estimates alone, it appears that homes
28:856:62628:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:recommended to Hispanic/LatinX buyers may be moderately less expensive than those
28:857:62709:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:recommended to their white counterparts, but that African American and Asian buyers
28:858:62792:22:22:99:442:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:receive recommendations that may somewhat more expensive on average.
28:859:62860:22:22:115:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:We perform an additional test to rule out this potential mechanism in Appendix
28:860:62938:22:21:99:511:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:Table24. Three columns correspond to each neighborhood characteristic in this table
28:861:63021:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:– for each characteristic, the third column incorporates an additional control into the
28:862:63108:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:main regression specification that measures the average neighborhood characteristic for
28:863:63195:22:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:all houses in the sample that fall in the same $20,000 price bin as the recommended
28:864:63278:22:21:99:511:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:house.31We are therefore testing whether, within a set of houses of similar price, are
28:865:63364:21:22:99:511:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:minority testers recommended houses with systematically di↵erent attributes. The main
28:866:63449:22:22:99:372:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:results in our table are invariant to this additional control.
28:867:63511:22:22:115:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, the steering behavior that we observe could also be driven by a form of statis-
28:868:63599:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:tical discrimination where real estate agents believe that the preferences of an individual
28:869:63690:22:21:99:510:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:buyer are the same as those of other members of their racial group. Alternatively, agents
28:870:63779:21:23:99:510:136:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:could simply believe that buyers have a preference for neighborhoods with households
28:871:63863:23:14:96:511:113:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:30In other results, we do not find evidence of clear di↵erences in steering behavior among real estate
28:872:63965:14:8:99:510:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:agents of the same group as the buyer (versus di↵erent group). Results available in an online appendix.
28:873:64068:8:14:96:511:91:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:31Note that limitations on our ability to match scraped school quality and assault data to the HUD data
28:874:64171:14:0:99:496:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:reduce our sample size by enough that we cannot perform this test for those two outcome variables.
29:875:64271:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:from their own race group.  Real estate agents that employ these forms of statistical
29:876:64356:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:discrimination rely more heavily upon the demographic composition of a neighborhood
29:877:64439:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:than the information provided about the preferences of an individual tester. We test for
29:878:64527:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:this behavior in a set of specifications that regress the racial composition (share of white,
29:879:64620:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:black, Hispanic/LatinX, or Asian households) of the recommended neighborhood on the
29:880:64703:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:interaction between tester race and the share of white households in the neighborhood of
29:881:64791:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the advertised listing presented to an agent. Table11 presents results from these tests,
29:882:64879:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:with the four columns pertaining to the respective share of white, black, Hispanic/LatinX,
29:883:64969:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and Asian households in the neighborhood of the recommended home. The results show
29:884:65051:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:that the steering e↵ect is stronger for African American buyers who present listings in
29:885:65138:22:22:99:511:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhoods with a higher percentage of white households. The e↵ect is of the same
29:886:65222:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sign but not as large and is not significant for Hispanic/LatinX buyers. Not only do we
29:887:65309:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:find that real estate agents do not take into account own-race preferences of African Amer-
29:888:65400:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ican buyers when making recommendations – they actively work in opposition to those
29:889:65483:22:42:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:preferences. This implies a mechanism that goes beyond simple statistical discrimination.
29:890:65572:42:29:99:440:355:171:g_d0_f2:171:g_d0_f2:C:6.5  The Welfare E↵ects of Discriminatory Behavior
29:891:65622:29:22:99:510:326:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:The results described above provide evidence that minorities receive housing recommen-
29:892:65708:22:22:99:510:304:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:dations in neighborhoods that could disadvantage them in numerous dimensions. The
29:893:65789:22:21:99:511:282:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:magnitude of the e↵ect of housing discrimination also depends on the information, pref-
29:894:65876:21:22:99:511:261:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:erences, and behavior of buyers. Therefore, obtaining precise estimates of welfare e↵ects
29:895:65965:22:22:99:510:239:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:would require an experiment that examines discriminatory behavior within the context of
29:896:66052:22:22:99:510:217:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:real preferences of individuals making decisions in a housing market. This would clearly
29:897:66140:22:21:99:305:195:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:be an undesirable experiment to implement.
29:898:66182:21:22:115:510:174:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:We expect that some buyers may be less informed about pollution exposures, school
29:899:66263:22:22:99:510:152:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:quality, or public safety in the neighborhoods where they are searching. In a review of
29:900:66350:22:22:99:511:130:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the evidence on locational choice and persistent inequality,Currie(2011) discusses the
29:901:66436:22:22:99:511:108:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:potential e↵ects of educational disparities in determining locational choices near Super-
29:902:66525:22:0:99:510:86:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:fund cleanups or plants with publicly disclosed emissions of toxic chemicals. Our results
30:903:66616:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:suggest that if buyers who lack information are more likely to be steered by their real
30:904:66703:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:estate agent, then minority buyers are likely to be di↵erentially steered and subsequently
30:905:66793:22:21:99:168:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:disadvantaged.
30:906:66807:21:22:115:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:In order to more directly compare our results on discrimination with the findings
30:907:66888:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:fromCurrie(2011), we restrict the HDS sample to mothers and construct a test of homes
30:908:66973:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:recommended to white versus African American mothers within 2 km of Superfund sites
30:909:67056:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:(that had not been cleaned up in 2011).Currie(2011) finds that 1.74% of all mothers
30:910:67139:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:live within 2 km of a Superfund site and that African American mothers are +0.77
30:911:67219:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points more likely to live within 2 km of a Superfund site, indicating a 43%
30:912:67306:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:di↵erence in the likelihood of maternal exposures between the groups. In our HDS sample
30:913:67393:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of cities with large minority populations, 24% of homes recommended to the sample of
30:914:67477:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mothers fall within 2 km of a Superfund site. The test indicates that African American
30:915:67563:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mothers are 10 percentage points more likely to receive a recommendation within 2km
30:916:67646:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of a Superfund site (estimate is significant at p<.1), indicating a 42.5% higher likelihood
30:917:67737:22:22:99:511:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:than their white counterpart. These estimates suggest that the di↵erences in maternal
30:918:67822:22:22:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:exposures from residential location could be entirely explained by discriminatory steering
30:919:67912:22:21:99:354:353:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:into homes that are within 2 km of a Superfund site.32
30:920:67966:21:22:115:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:To provide additional context for our results, considerChetty et al.(2016), who
30:921:68045:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:analyze the Moving to Opportunity (MTO) experimental voucher program. The MTO
30:922:68122:22:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:program provided vouchers for residents living in neighborhoods with a poverty rate of
30:923:68208:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:greater than 40% to obtain subsidies in neighborhoods with poverty rates of less than
30:924:68293:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:10%.Chetty et al.(2016) find that the treatment was responsible for a 17 percentage
30:925:68376:22:22:99:510:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:point (intent to treat) or 36 percentage point (treatment on the treated) reduction in
30:926:68462:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhood poverty and subsequent impacts of this poverty reduction on income, college
30:927:68550:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:education, employment, marriage and fertility later in life. In the HDS sample, only 1% of
30:928:68640:22:21:99:510:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:recommended homes are in neighborhoods with poverty rates of greater than 40%, making
30:929:68725:21:23:99:510:136:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:it di-cult to draw a direct comparison with a statistically powered test for the high
30:930:68810:23:14:96:510:113:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:32We construct a similar test of di↵erences in air toxics using our RSEI measure. On average, homes
30:931:68909:14:11:99:510:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:recommended to mothers in the HDS study have a RSEI level of 5313.1.  Homes recommended to
30:932:68999:11:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:African American mothers have levels that are 2268.9 higher (estimate is significant at p<.1) than their
30:933:69103:11:0:99:341:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:white counterpart, indicating a 42.6% disparity in exposures.
31:934:69166:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:poverty neighborhoods. Rather, a test of steering into low poverty block groups as defined
31:935:69256:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:by MTO33indicates that minority testers are 6% less likely to be recommended a home in
31:936:69342:22:21:99:511:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:these neighborhoods (significant at p<.1). African American testers are 6.3% less likely
31:937:69430:21:22:99:511:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:(not significant at p<.1) and Hispanic/LatinX testers are 11.1% less likely (significant at
31:938:69521:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:p<.05). African American testers with families are 12.1% less likely (not significant at
31:939:69609:22:22:99:511:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:p<.1) and Latino testers with families are 22.6% less likely to receive recommendations
31:940:69696:22:21:99:511:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in neighborhoods with low poverty rates (significant at p<.1).34There are caveats with
31:941:69782:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:this comparison. In particular, we isolate the e↵ect of housing discrimination occurring
31:942:69870:22:22:99:511:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in a single stage of the housing search process; the steering e↵ect that we identify is
31:943:69957:22:22:99:511:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:therefore likely a lower bound on the e↵ect of total discrimination, though these estimates
31:944:70048:22:22:99:511:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f9:B:suggest that the impacts of discriminatory steering are bothstatisticallyandeconomically
31:945:70136:22:21:99:157:462:119:g_d0_f3:53:g_d0_f5:B:significant.35
31:946:70150:21:22:115:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:For buyers who lack information about pollution exposures or other neighborhood
31:947:70229:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:attributes, adverse welfare impacts are likely to come directly from the short and long-run
31:948:70320:22:22:99:511:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:outcomes associated with multiple neighborhood e↵ects. Another type of buyer may be
31:949:70403:22:21:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:well-informed, but may not have strong preferences for the neighborhood and pollution
31:950:70488:21:22:99:510:354:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics that we examine in this study.  The strength of individual preferences
31:951:70574:22:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:will determine the e↵ects in our model of expected utility. However, it is important to
31:952:70661:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:note that a minority buyer that does not have strong preferences for the neighborhood
31:953:70746:22:22:99:511:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics that we study will nonetheless experience di↵erent outcomes than a white
31:954:70834:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:buyer with the exact same preferences. Assuming that these buyers are more likely to
31:955:70918:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:be steered into neighborhoods with higher levels of poverty and pollution exposures,
31:956:71002:22:22:99:391:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:discriminatory steering will put them at a direct disadvantage.
31:957:71065:22:22:115:511:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:For buyers who are well-informed about pollution exposures and neighborhood e↵ects,
31:958:71148:22:22:99:511:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:discriminatory behavior will interact with preferences to produce an e↵ect on expected
31:959:71234:22:15:96:511:157:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:33We define the MTO-consistent measure as a recommended home in a census block group where the
31:960:71328:15:7:99:348:142:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:share of families living below the poverty line is less than 10%.
31:961:71393:7:11:96:379:135:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:34Full panel of results from this comparison are available upon request.
31:962:71465:11:14:96:510:124:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:35Yinger(1997) examines the total e↵ect of discrimination on the surplus from a housing search, including
31:963:71570:14:11:99:510:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:di↵erences in assistance and encouragement, assistance with a loan application, and loan approval. The
31:964:71672:11:11:99:511:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:e↵ects of discriminatory steering into higher poverty neighborhoods estimated in this study could be
31:965:71772:11:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:compounded by di↵erences in information provided by a real estate agent about neighborhood conditions,
31:966:71874:11:0:99:510:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:di↵erences in recommendations regarding an initial o↵er, or di↵erences during the process of negotiations.
32:967:71982:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:utility.  For instance, home buyers may sort on race, and minority buyers may pre-
32:968:72064:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:fer houses in neighborhoods populated by other minorities. We see from Figure 3 that
32:969:72148:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhood poverty, college education, high skill and school quality are all strongly
32:970:72235:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:correlated with race (although the same is less evident for assaults, Superfund proximity,
32:971:72325:22:22:99:511:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and air toxics). Without knowing the relative strengths of preferences for di↵erent neigh-
32:972:72415:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:borhood attributes (including the racial mix of one’s neighbors) we are unable to know for
32:973:72505:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sure how the attributes of houses recommended by real estate agents interact to produce
32:974:72592:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:expected utility.36Returning to the model in Section 4, we can, however, say something
32:975:72678:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:about the impact of agent behavior on the welfare of whites and minorities from housing
32:976:72765:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:search. In particular, the incorporation of the tester’sindividualpreferences by a real
32:977:72852:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:estate agent, expressed by the information inherent in her “choice” of advertised house,
32:978:72940:22:21:99:511:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f9:B:will unambiguously increase that tester’s expected utility from housing search,ceteris
32:979:73026:21:22:99:511:441:119:g_d0_f9:119:g_d0_f3:B:paribus. Our data do allow us to test directly the extent to which this individual infor-
32:980:73115:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:mation is incorporated into the recommendations of real estate agents, and in particular
32:981:73203:22:22:99:240:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:how this di↵ers by tester race.
32:982:73234:22:22:115:511:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Table12 reports estimates that test for these di↵erences.  For each recommended
32:983:73313:22:21:99:511:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:house attribute, a coe-cient describes the interaction of the tester’s race with the corre-
32:984:73404:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:sponding attribute value for the tester’s advertised house. We see first that whites, who
32:985:73493:22:22:99:510:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:are the omitted racial group, have a strong positive and statistically significant relation-
32:986:73585:22:22:99:510:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ship between each recommended house attribute and their preference for that attribute
32:987:73670:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:expressed through their advertised house.  For African Americans, this relationship is
32:988:73756:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:significantly weakened for every neighborhood attribute with the exception of Superfund
32:989:73843:22:22:99:510:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:proximity. Hispanic testers have a significantly weaker relationship in the case of high
32:990:73931:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:skill, school quality and air toxics, and Asian testers have a weaker relationship in the case
32:991:74025:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of assaults and all of the pollution variables. In the case of poverty, high skill and college
32:992:74119:22:15:96:511:157:40:g_d0_f6:82:g_d0_f7:F:36The seemingly obvious solution to this problem would be to estimate preferences for buyers of di↵erent
32:993:74223:15:10:99:510:142:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:race groups from observed housing transactions data – indeed, this is done commonly in the hedonics and
32:994:74326:10:11:99:510:132:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:residential sorting literatures. We highlight here, however, that such estimates will themselves likely be
32:995:74432:11:11:99:511:121:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:contaminated by constraints imposed by real estate agents of the sort discribed above. Put di↵erently,
32:996:74534:11:11:99:510:110:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:discrimination is likely already “baked in” to utility parameters derived from revealed preference data.
32:997:74638:11:11:99:510:99:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:This is a broader problem for work in non-market valuation and allocation of funds to the provision of
32:998:74740:11:11:99:510:88:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:public goods; in the current context, it makes it di-cult to draw strong conclusions about welfare e↵ects
32:999:74845:11:0:99:154:77:82:g_d0_f7:82:g_d0_f7:F:from steering.
33:1000:74861:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:education, Asian testers exhibit a stronger relationship than their white counterpart, and
33:1001:74951:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the same is true in the case of assaults for Hispanic testers. However, particularly for
33:1002:75039:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:African Americans, individual preferences are ignored by real estate agents relative to
33:1003:75126:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the case of whites. This leads to a relative reduction in expected utility from the search
33:1004:75216:22:50:99:136:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:process.
33:1005:75224:50:32:99:217:565:246:g_d0_f2:246:g_d0_f2:C:7  Conclusions
33:1006:75238:32:22:99:510:533:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:In this paper, we find strong evidence that contact with real estate agents di↵erentially
33:1007:75327:22:22:99:510:511:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:constrains the choice sets of minority buyers relative to a white counterpart. Building on
33:1008:75417:22:21:99:511:489:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:prior literature, we show that while discrimination no longer has a significant e↵ect on
33:1009:75505:21:22:99:510:468:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the number of recommendations a minority buyer receives, it does have strong impacts on
33:1010:75592:22:22:99:510:446:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the quality of the neighborhoods that constitute the recommended set. The implications
33:1011:75678:22:22:99:510:424:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of these constraints are quite clear – the constraints imposed by real estate agents in the
33:1012:75769:22:22:99:510:402:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:search process provide all minority groups with houses to choose from that are worse in
33:1013:75856:22:21:99:311:380:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:at least one (but typically many) dimensions.
33:1014:75901:21:22:115:510:359:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:This is a result with implications for several literatures in economics.  First, it is
33:1015:75987:22:22:99:511:337:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:important for studies of “neighborhood e↵ects”, which analyze the ways in which neigh-
33:1016:76073:22:22:99:511:315:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:borhood attributes a↵ect short and long-run (even multi-generational) outcomes in the
33:1017:76158:22:22:99:510:293:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:dimensions of poverty, employment, schooling, criminal activity and public safety, and
33:1018:76244:22:21:99:510:271:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:environmental health. Prior research has demonstrated clearly that residential location
33:1019:76331:21:22:99:511:250:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:choices can a↵ect short- and long-run outcomes; the steering behavior that we identify
33:1020:76417:22:22:99:511:228:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:a↵ects the neighborhood attributes in the household’s choice set, and ultimately their
33:1021:76503:22:22:99:314:206:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:house purchase decision, in an important way.
33:1022:76548:22:21:115:510:184:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Second, our results demonstrate that minority homebuyers and renters may not be
33:1023:76627:21:22:98:511:163:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:“free to choose”in the housing market, and that their observed behavior may not actually
33:1024:76715:22:22:99:510:141:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:reveal their preferences. If households’ choice sets are distorted by the recommendations
33:1025:76804:22:22:99:510:119:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:provided by real estate agents, this can have important implications for how we interpret
33:1026:76893:22:0:99:510:97:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the results of non-market valuation analyses and for how perceived preferences are used
34:1027:76982:0:22:99:510:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to allocate public goods. Our results suggest that what might look on face value to be
34:1028:77068:22:22:99:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:weak preferences for environmental quality on the part of minorities may actually be a
34:1029:77154:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:reflection of the fact that they were presented with options that were disproportionately
34:1030:77243:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:lower in environmental quality than were those given to similar white buyers. The results
34:1031:77332:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of non-market valuation studies based on supposedly unconstrained choices over housing
34:1032:77418:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:units are the backbone of cost-benefit analyses and evaluation of environmental policies
34:1033:77506:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in the US. They also play a critical role in determining how governments allocate scarce
34:1034:77594:21:22:99:380:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:funds to the provision of public services across communities.
34:1035:77655:22:22:115:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, our results provide evidence that even holding income disparities or di↵erences
34:1036:77743:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:in preferences constant, housing discrimination could play an important role in determin-
34:1037:77832:22:22:99:510:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ing observed spatial correlations between race, income, and local disamenities. This has
34:1038:77920:22:21:99:510:462:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:particularly important implications considering pollution, and policies relating to envi-
34:1039:78009:21:22:99:510:441:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:ronmental justice. Under an executive order signed by Bill Clinton in 1994, the federal
34:1040:78096:22:22:99:510:419:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:government is obligated to consider the distributional impacts of its policies with respect
34:1041:78187:22:22:99:510:397:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to pollution and disadvantaged groups. Understanding the origins of existing inequities
34:1042:78274:22:22:99:510:375:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:has been the topic of a large and growing literature (Banzhaf et al.,2018). Discrimination
34:1043:78364:22:21:99:510:353:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:has largely been overlooked by that literature, and our paper suggests that this may be
34:1044:78451:21:22:99:510:332:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:an important oversight. This particular mechanism has important implications for the
34:1045:78535:22:22:99:254:310:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:development of fair housing laws.
34:1046:78568:22:22:115:511:288:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:While we are able to identify the di↵erential impacts of real estate agents on the
34:1047:78650:22:21:99:510:266:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:housing search processes of whites and minorities, we note that the HUD audit data
34:1048:78732:21:22:99:510:245:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:do not allow for direct tests of the behavioral mechanisms underlying these e↵ects. We
34:1049:78818:22:22:99:511:223:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:find that the di↵erential constraints imposed by agents occur irrespective of preferences
34:1050:78907:22:22:99:510:201:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:demonstrated by testers in the form of their “choice” of advertised house, though we
34:1051:78991:22:22:99:510:179:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:cannot disentangle mechanisms based on statistical discrimination from others based on,
34:1052:79078:22:21:99:510:157:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:for example, racial animus or disregarding financial credentials. We propose an expanded
34:1053:79166:21:22:99:510:136:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:research agenda in the economics of housing discrimination, including complementary
34:1054:79249:22:22:99:510:114:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:experimental designs that are capable of more directly testing the behavioral mechanisms
34:1055:79337:22:0:99:511:92:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:underlying discriminatory steering as inKnowles et al.(2001),List(2004), andCharles
35:1056:79422:0:22:99:191:702:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:and Guryan(2008).
35:1057:79439:22:22:115:510:680:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:A:Perhaps an even more important avenue for experimental research involves the design
35:1058:79522:22:21:99:510:658:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:of a research methodology that combines experimental identification of discriminatory
35:1059:79607:21:22:99:510:637:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:behavior with individual preferences that are representative of decisions being made in
35:1060:79694:22:22:99:510:615:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:the housing market. These could be used to obtain precise estimates of welfare e↵ects. An
35:1061:79783:22:22:99:510:593:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:important remaining question is the extent to which the constraints from discriminatory
35:1062:79870:22:21:99:510:571:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:steering may be overcome by tenacity – buyers with a su-ciently high marginal utility
35:1063:79955:21:22:99:510:550:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:for certain housing characteristics may choose to absorb additional search costs in order
35:1064:80044:22:22:99:510:528:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:to expand their choice set.  Unfortunately, studying this aspect is not possible in the
35:1065:80131:22:22:99:510:506:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:audit study context. Neither is a study of the mortgage lending process, where we might
35:1066:80218:22:0:99:443:484:119:g_d0_f3:119:g_d0_f3:B:expect the sorts of discriminatory e↵ects we identify here to be amplified.
